03/09/21, 09:10 - Avinash: Aur ek idea hai pr advance hai cpp to python language convertor bana sakte hai
03/09/21, 09:10 - Avinash: Kya
03/09/21, 09:10 - Avinash: ?
03/09/21, 09:12 - Teknath Jha: Kyu per
03/09/21, 09:13 - Teknath Jha: Complexity to bad rahi hai yaha pe
03/09/21, 09:13 - Avinash: All common programming languages are Turing complete, which means there‚Äôs nothing one programming language does that another can‚Äôt. All programming language can achieve the same algorithms, can solve the same problems, and give the same result if their programs are identical. Therefore, it‚Äôs completely possible to convert C++ code to Python.

In the real world, however, this isn‚Äôt as easy to do. What you‚Äôre looking for is a transpiler, which takes a program from one language to another. As Patrick answered in a different response to this question, C++ and Python have significant paradigm differences that went into the language design which affects the ability to port code from one to another. Probably the trickiest part is that Python is a higher level language than C/C++, and doesn‚Äôt have the ability to directly address memory like Python does (Patrick touches on this when mentioning memset()/memcpy()). As thus, transpilers typically do their best to bridge the abstraction gap, which typically fails or makes faulty assumptions.

For example, here‚Äôs a simple C program, which I then tried transpiling to Python manually

#include <stdio.h> 
 
int main(){ 
	char* a = "Hello world"; 
	printf("%s", a); 
	return 0 
} 
_

def main(): 
	a = "Hello world" 
	print(a) 
	return 0 
The obvious problem with my literal transpiling, for one, is the programs have different outputs. My C program automatically runs main, as a feature of the C language, while my Python just has a function declaration which is never called. I suppose a smart transpiler will call the function, or use a class with an __init__ function, but then it wouldn‚Äôt be a literal transpiling anymore. You can also run into more issues with type calling, memory access issues, and more, which Patrick explained very well in his own answer.

Hope this helped!

verification at institute level and sometime they also missed deadlines
of availing scholarships .
We develop a website "Doc Tracker" which will notify student to track their 
documents direct via our website, they will be notified via emails on each 
successive stages of document .
This website will help  to short out the communication between authority and 
student . Student will not miss their scholarship.
College staff will be able to direct contact to student to get work done.

13/09/21, 10:16 - Avinash: Dear Students,
To appear for the exam kindly use the below link:-
http://wcoe.unionline.in

Checklist/Requirement : 
1. Mobile phone / laptop / PC with working front camera as Web cam. 
2. Make sure your using updated browser such as (Chrome or Mozilla Firefox)
-Username is your enrollment no.
-Password is your mobile number
- Upload your Admit Card/recent passport size photo for Face Recognition process.
- Keep the scanned image ready for uploading during the authentication process. Store it on desktop or File Manager if using Mobile Phone.
- The system will match your Photo along with your Hall ticket.
-Must have an active internet connection.
-Also make sure your mobile or laptop is fully charged.
-Keep required stationery handy with you (pencil, pen, rough sheet etc.)
- Make sure your browser is allowed to access Camera to avoid Camera error.

Note- Do not write answers in the empty box given below the question your answers won't be considered.
Instead write on a piece of paper and upload answers using the select file button

13/09/21, 10:56 - Teknath Jha: Customers are WCE faculty and students...
13/09/21, 10:56 - Teknath Jha: There may be 3-4 desks a file/document may travel ...we need to understand source sender ..to destination (To whom ) and intermediate desks till work is not done sequences...So need to consider use cases ...for eg "a faculty submits document through HoD to Director for sanction of bills (some work done)" ...then sequences are as 1. faculty submits to HoD...2. HoD signs recommends and sent it through a peon book to Office inward section ...it is acknowledged in the peon book as received with timestamp (date/time )...then it goes to registrar ...second ack needed here with timestamp ..then he assigns it to concerned section clerk ..third ack needed here with timestamp...then when that work done it goes to registrar ...fourth ack needed ..then registrar submits it to director using a book entry...fifth ack needed...then when done from director again it comes to registrar ...sixth ack needed and then it goes to Accounts Officer....seventh ack required ...then to cashier ...eighth ack needed ...and finally notification is required for sender like SMS that the work is done

16/09/21, 22:45 - Avinash: When students or faculties sends any document to institution in form reports, bills, proposals or request then it has to go through several stages to reach responsible authority for any verification or approval. In this period sender has no idea about the status of document. Sender has to check several times by going into office that, is there are any issues or it has been approved sucessfully.it becomes very difficult for sender to track the document.
     To overcome this problem we have created one application that will help to user  track document submitted to institution. We will notify current status of document to user via email, SMS on each stage and according to that user will report the institution. In this way we will save the time ,reduce efforts of user  and  make process faster.
16/09/21, 22:46 - Avinash: Students have been facing problems in tracking their documents for 
verification at institute level and sometime they also missed deadlines
of availing scholarships .
We develop a website "Doc Tracker" which will notify student to track their 
documents direct via our website, they will be notified via emails on each 
successive stages of document .
This website will help  to short out the communication between authority and 
student . Student will not miss their scholarship.
College staff will be able to direct contact to student to get work done.    @919323451278's abstract

08/10/21, 20:20 - Sanap Aditya: # Name : Harshal Kodgire
# PRN : 2019BTECS00029
# Batch : T6

# Apply Goal Stack Planning technique to solve block world problem.

tab = []
result = []
goalList = ["a", "b", "c", "d", "e"]


def parSolution(N):
    for i in range(N):
        if goalList[i] != result[i]:
            return False
    return True


def Onblock(index, count):

    # break point of recursive call
    if count == len(goalList)+1:
        return True
    # copy tab of index value to result
    block = tab[index]
    # stack block
    result.append(block)
    print(result)
    if parSolution(count):
        print("Pushed a result solution ")
        # remove block from tab
        tab.remove(block)
        Onblock(0, count + 1)
    else:
        print("result solution not possible, back to the tab")
        # pop out if no partial solution
        result.pop()
        Onblock(index+1, count)


def Ontab(problem):
    # check if everything in stack is on the tab
    if len(problem) != 0:
        tab.append(problem.pop())
        Ontab(problem)
    # if everything is on the tab the we return true
    else:
        return True


def goal_stack_planing(problem):
    # pop problem and put in tab
    Ontab(problem)
    # print index and number of blocks on result stack
    if Onblock(0, 1):
        print(result)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    problem = ["c", "a", "e", "d", "b"]
    print("Goal Problem")
    for k, j in zip(goalList, problem):
        print(k+"    "+j)
    goal_stack_planing(problem)
    print("result Solution")
    print(result)

23/11/21, 07:41 - Avinash: import streamlit as st
import pickle
import numpy as np

# import the model
pipe = pickle.load(open('pipe.pkl','rb'))
df = pickle.load(open('df.pkl','rb'))

st.title("Laptop Predictor")

# brand
company = st.selectbox('Brand',df['Company'].unique())

# type of laptop
type = st.selectbox('Type',df['TypeName'].unique())

# Ram
ram = st.selectbox('RAM(in GB)',df['Ram'].unique())

# weight
weight = st.selectbox('Weight of the Laptop(kg)',[1.0,1.5,1.75,2.0,2.5,3,3.5])

# Touchscreen
touchscreen = st.selectbox('Touchscreen',['No','Yes'])

# IPS
ips = st.selectbox('IPS',['No','Yes'])

# screen size
screen_size = st.selectbox('Screen Size',[14,14.5,15,15.6,16,17,17.3])

# resolution
resolution = st.selectbox('Screen Resolution',['1920x1080','1366x768','1600x900','3840x2160','3200x1800','2880x1800','2560x1600','2560x1440','2304x1440'])

#cpu
cpu = st.selectbox('CPU',df['Cpu brand'].unique())

hdd = st.selectbox('HDD(in GB)',[500,1000,2000])

ssd = st.selectbox('SSD(in GB)',[0,8,128,256,512,1024])

gpu = st.selectbox('GPU',df['Gpu brand'].unique())

os = st.selectbox('OS',df['os'].unique())

if st.button('Predict Price'):
    # query
    ppi = None
    if touchscreen == 'Yes':
        touchscreen = 1
    else:
        touchscreen = 0

    if ips == 'Yes':
        ips = 1
    else:
        ips = 0

    X_res = int(resolution.split('x')[0])
    Y_res = int(resolution.split('x')[1])
    ppi = ((X_res**2) + (Y_res**2))**0.5/screen_size
    query = np.array([company,type,ram,weight,touchscreen,ips,ppi,cpu,hdd,ssd,gpu,os])

    query = query.reshape(1,12)
    st.title("The predicted price of this configuration is " + str(int(np.exp(pipe.predict(query)[0]))))

24/11/21, 19:59 - Avinash: function validate() {  
	var result = "";	
	result += validateName(); 	
	result += validateEmail();
	result += validatePassword();
	result += validateTerms();
	
	if (result == "") return true;
	
	alert("Validation Result:\n\n" + result);
	return false;	
}

function validateName() {
	var name = document.getElementsByName("name")[0].value;
	if (name.length <= 3)
		return "Name should be at least three characters.\n";	
	return "";
}

function validatePassword() {
	var password = valueOf("password");
	var retype = valueOf("retype_password");
	
	if (password.length <= 6) 
		return "Password should be at least 6 characters.\n";
	
	if (password != retype) 
		return "Passwords do not match.\n";	
	return "";
}

function validateEmail() {
	var email = valueOf("email");
	var retype = valueOf("retype_email");
	
	if (email.indexOf('@') == -1) 
		return "Email should be a valid address.\n";
	
	if (email != retype)
		return "Email addresses do not match.\n";
	return "";	
}

function validateTerms() {
	var terms = document.getElementsByName("terms")[0];
	if (!terms.checked)
		return "Please accept the Terms of Service and Privacy Policy";	
	return "";
}

function valueOf(name) {
	return document.getElementsByName(name)[0].value;
}

19/03/22, 00:22 - Teknath Jha: Currently in schools teachers perform manual work to prepare and track students learning‚Äôs outcome through report cards. This is the standard procedure done manually throughout the country. Often it is observed that students are also good in co-curricular activities and being good in academics is not the only way ahead. In current situation it is not possible for a teacher to pay attention to every student and find out the best in a child. Hence there is a need to develop solutions to track all activities of a student including the academic progress in real-time. Innovation in this domain will be appreciated to develop systems which automatically reads the students progress and generates feedback also is a good way to proceed.
